   <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="640">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> </td> 
   <td>Most workers are covered by an <a href="/wiki/Industrial_award" title="Industrial award">award</a>, which may vary by employee age, geographical location and industry. Workers receive mandatory employer <a href="/wiki/Superannuation_in_Australia" title="Superannuation in Australia">superannuation contributions</a> of at least 9.5% of wages, alongside loadings such as penalty rates or leave loading. Minimum wages are set federally by the <a href="/wiki/Fair_Work_Commission" title="Fair Work Commission">Fair Work Commission</a>. <p>For those 21 and older, not covered by an award or other instrument, the minimum wages is <a href="/wiki/Australian_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Dollar">A$</a>753.80 ($535.63 USD) per week, or <a href="/wiki/Australian_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Dollar">A$</a>19.84 ($15.36 USD) per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-Fair_Work_Ombudsman_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fair_Work_Ombudsman-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Casual_employment_(contract)#Australia" title="Casual employment (contract)">Casual workers</a> are paid a loading of typically 25%, resulting in a minimum of <a href="/wiki/Australian_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Dollar">A$</a>24.80 per hour for those workers. </p><p>Workers under 21, apprentices and trainees not covered by an award, have a minimum wages set at a percentage of the ordinary rate.<sup id="cite_ref-Fair_Work_Ombudsman_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fair_Work_Ombudsman-21">[21]</a></sup> For those under 16, this is 36.8% or <a href="/wiki/Australian_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Dollar">A$</a>7.30 per hour; <a href="/wiki/Australian_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Dollar">A$</a>9.13 with the casual loading.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> </td> 
   <td><span data-sort-value="7004280340000000000♠">28,034</span> </td>

   <td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> </td> 
   <td>None; National collective bargaining agreements set minimum wages by job classification for each industry and provide for a minimum wage of <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>1,200 ($1,289) per month<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (August 2018)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:List_of_countries_by_minimum_wage#Dubious" title="Talk:List of countries by minimum wage">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup>. Wages where no such collective agreements exist, such as for domestic workers, janitorial staff and au pairs, are regulated by relevant legislation and are generally lower than those covered by collective bargaining. The national minimum wage legislation has lapsed, although is still in force by convention.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CRHRP-2012_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRHRP-2012-8">[8]</a></sup> </td>
